# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've successfully identified all Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that implement web UI authentication controls. The analysis is complete and saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

### Key Findings:

**Three Authentication Mechanisms:**

1. **BasicAuth Middleware** - Implemented via `github.com/prometheus/exporter-toolkit/web` package, configured through `--web.config.file` with `basic_auth_users` containing bcrypt-hashed passwords

2. **TLS Client Certificate Validation** - Also via exporter-toolkit, configured in web config file with `tls_server_config`, `client_auth_type`, and `client_ca_file` for mutual TLS

3. **Admin API Access Control** - Implemented in `web/api/v1/api.go` with the `enableAdmin` flag checked in admin endpoint functions (`deleteSeries`, `cleanTombstones`, `snapshot`)

**Key Files:**
- `web/web.go` - Main web server handler that calls toolkit_web.ServeMultiple()
- `web/api/v1/api.go` - API struct with enableAdmin field and admin endpoint implementations
- `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - Command-line flag definitions
- `util/httputil/*.go` - Supporting HTTP utilities for CORS, context, and compression

The answer file includes the files, key symbols, execution chain, and a detailed narrative explaining the authentication flow and security boundaries.

net/http (see https://github.com/go-kit/kit/issues/233).\n123: func withStackTracer(h http.Handler, l *slog.Logger) http.Handler {\n124: \treturn http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\n125: \t\tdefer func() {\n126: \t\t\tif err := recover(); err != nil {\n127: \t\t\t\tconst size = 64 << 10\n128: \t\t\t\tbuf := make([]byte, size)\n129: \t\t\t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n130: \t\t\t\tl.Error(\"panic while serving request\", \"client\", r.RemoteAddr, \"url\", r.URL, \"err\", err, \"stack\", buf)\n131: \t\t\t\tpanic(err)\n132: \t\t\t}\n133: \t\t}()\n134: \t\th.ServeHTTP(w, r)\n135: \t})\n136: }\n137: \n138: type metrics struct {\n139: \trequestCounter  *prometheus.CounterVec\n140: \trequestDuration Web Server Setup (web/web.go)\\nThe Handler struct in web/web.go serves as the main HTTP server:\\n- The `Run()` method (line 722) sets up the HTTP server with multiple listeners\\n- It calls `toolkit_web.ServeMultiple()` (line 760) which applies TLS and BasicAuth middleware from the exporter-toolkit\\n- The webConfig file path is passed to the toolkit: `&toolkit_web.FlagConfig{WebConfigFile: &webConfig}`\\n- The toolkit_web package from github.com/prometheus/exporter-toolkit/web handles:\\n  - TLS certificate loading and validation\\n  - Client certificate validation using the client_ca_file\\n  - BasicAuth middleware that validates username/password against bcrypt-hashed users\\n\\n#### 3. Admin API Access Control (web/api/v1/api.go)\\nThe API struct contains an `enableAdmin` field (line 241) that controls access to admin endpoints:\\n\\n**Admin API Endpoints:**\\n- `POST/PUT /admin/tsdb/delete_series` - Implemented by `deleteSeries()` function (line 2026)\\n- `POST/PUT /admin/tsdb/clean_tombstones` - Implemented by `cleanTombstones()` function (line 2093)\\n- `POST/PUT /admin/tsdb/snapshot` - Implemented by `snapshot()` function (line 2059)\\n\\nEach admin function checks `if !api.enableAdmin` at the beginning and returns an \\\"admin APIs disabled\\\" error if the flag is not set.\\n\\nThe `NewAPI()` function (line 267) accepts the `enableAdmin` parameter and stores it in the API struct. This parameter is set from the `--web.enable-admin-api` flag in main.go.\\n\\n#### 4. HTTP Utilities (util/httputil/)\\nThe httputil package provides supporting functionality:\\n- `cors.go`: CORS header handling via `SetCORS()` function\\n- `context.go`: Request context utilities\\n- `compression.go`: Request/response compression handling\\n\\n### Authentication Flow\\n\\n1. **Request arrives at web server** \u2192 `web/web.go:Run()` handles listening\\n2. **TLS/BasicAuth applied** \u2192 `toolkit_web.ServeMultiple()` middleware validates client certs and basic auth credentials\\n3. **Request routed to API** \u2192 Routes registered in `web/api/v1/api.go:Register()`\\n4. **Admin API access checked** \u2192 Functions check `api.enableAdmin` flag and return 503 error if disabled\\n5. **Response returned** \u2192 Includes CORS headers if configured\\n\\n### Configuration Example\\n\\nWeb configuration file format (referenced by `--web.config.file`):\\n```yaml\\ntls_server_config:\\n  cert_file: server.crt\\n  key_file: server.key\\n  client_auth_type: \\\"RequireAndVerifyClientCert\\\"\\n  client_ca_file: client_ca.crt\\n\\nbasic_auth_users:\\n  alice: $2y$10$mDwo.lAisC94iLAyP81MCesa29IzH37oigHC/42V2pdJlUprsJPze\\n```\\n\\nCommand-line invocation:\\n```bash\\nprometheus --web.config.file=/etc/prometheus/web-config.yml --web.enable-admin-api\\n```\\n\\n### Security Boundaries\\n\\nThe implementation follows these security patterns:\\n1. **TLS and BasicAuth are enforced at the HTTP server level** via the exporter-toolkit, protecting all endpoints\\n2. **Admin API is additionally gated by the enableAdmin flag** at the application level, requiring explicit opt-in\\n3. **CORS is configurable** to prevent unauthorized cross-origin access\\n4. **Client certificate validation** is supported for mutual TLS authentication between Prometheus and clients\\n\"\n}\n",
